FORM 28 
 
SUPPORT SERVICES 
 
The University provides the students with several support services. This includes the Office of the 
Vice Chancellor for Student Services, Guidance and Counselling Center, the Medical and Dental 
Health Services, the Office of Safety and Security Services,  the Graduate Do rmitory. There are 
also available scholarships and financial aid. Below are the brief description of each services. 
 
Student Services 
 
To augment and supplement the students’ academic training, the following services are provided 
for the students: 
 
Office of the Vice Chancellor for Student Services 
 
The Office of the Vice Chancellor for Student Services was created under BOR Resolution No. 
50, series of 2019 which was anchored on the CHED Memorandum Order No.09 s. 2013 - 
Enhanced policies and Guidelin es on Student Affairs and Services. The office intends to be one 
stop office that will address students concerns. 
 
The office provides a set of student – centered activities and services in support of academic 
instruction intended to facilitate holistic and well-rounded student development. 
 
Office Core/Main Functions: 
 
The OVCSS will supervise and monitor all offices under to this cluster. It will oversee all activities 
pertaining to students and student services that include, but are not necessarily limited to the 
following – scholarships; learning assistance and tutorials; guidance and counseling; student 
complaints; student housing (dormitories); student organizations; student discipline; and food and 
health services. 
 
Guidance and Counselling Center  
 
The Guidance and Counselling Center (GCC) provides essential services to each student including 
graduate student in achieving self-realization by enabling a student to dynamically understand 
him/herself in relation to his/her social psychol ogical world. Programs and services include 
individual inventory services, counselling, testing, information services, placement service, follow  
up service and enrichm ent activities e.g. exploration , effective study habits, coping with stress, 
pre-employment seminar etc. They also offer online counselling during the COVID 19 pandemic. 
 
 
Medical and Dental Health Services 
 
The office offers Medical, Nursing, Laboratory and Dental Services to all students and employees 
of the Institute. The laboratory offers primary and secondary laboratory services and waits for the 
DOH accreditation. The Institute clinic has 5 beds to cater in-patients for a day-admission, and has 
an ambulance to ferry sick students and employees to the nearby hospitals. 
 
Office of Safety and Security Services 
 
Checklist 28 

--- PAGE 114 ---
 
108 
 
The Office of Safety and Security Services provides for a safe and secure environment for all 
members of the academic community through strict implementation of university policies. 
 
Office of Residential and Food Services 
 
The office is responsible for the supervision of MSU -IIT’s residential units for graduate students 
(Graduate Dormitory) and official guest (Hostel). It handles matter pertaining to accommodation. 
The office also monitors the food service facilities in the campus such as canteens and refreshment 
stalls. 
 
Scholarships & Financial Aid 
 
A considerable number of students enrolled in the program have been granted scholarships by the 
University's longstanding collaborators: 
 
CHED-FDP 
 
The Commission on Higher Education – Faculty Development Program (CHED -FDP) is one of 
the flagship scholarships of CHED. The program aims to uplift the qualifications and competencies 
of faculty of higher education institutions. The scholarship provides assistance to faculty who want 
to obtain their masters or doctorate degrees. For more information on the scholarship, please refer 
to this website: http://www.ched.gov.ph/index.php/projects-programs/programs/faculty-
development-program/ 
 
CHED-SIKAP 
 
The Commission on Higher Education  - Scholarships for Instructors’ Knowledge Advancement 
Program (CHED-SIKAP) scholarship is a financial assistance program offered by CHED in the 
Philippines. It is specifically designed for university faculty members who want to pursue graduate 
studies. The scholarship aims to enhance the academic qualifications of faculty members and 
improve the quality of instruction in higher education institutions in the country. The program 
provides financial assistance to qualified faculty members, which covers tuition and other school-
related fees, transportation expenses, book allowances, and a monthly st ipend. Recipients of the 
scholarship are required to maintain good academic standing throughout the program and are 
expected to return to their respective institutions upon completion of their studies to serve as 
mentors and share their newly acquired knowledge and skills with their colleagues and students. 
 
Research Assistantship 
 
Research assistantship is awarded to graduate students who assist faculty members in conducting 
their research projects. In exchange for their assistance, research assistants rec eive a stipend or 
salary (PhP 15,208.80/month). 
 
The duties of a research assistant may vary depending on the specific project they are working on, 
but typically involve assisting with data collection, analysis, literature review, or administrative 
tasks related to the research project. 
 
Graduate students interested in pursuing a research assistantship should check with their academic 
department or the Department of Research for information on available opportunities and 
eligibility requirements.

MASTER OF SCIENCE IN COMPUTER APPLICATIONS 
 
 
Data Study for MSCA Program 
 
The Master of Science in Computer Applications is one of the approved programs from the ERDT 
scholarship program of DOST.  
 
The Engineering Research and  Development for Technology (ERDT) is a consortium of  eight 
member universities in the country that offer and doctoral degrees in various engineering  fields. 
This Consortium is composed of Ateneo  de Manila University (ADMU), Central Luzon  State 
University (CLSU), De La Salle University  (DLSU), Mapua University (MU), Mindanao  State 
University-Iligan Insti tute of Technology  (MSU-IIT), University of the Philippines Diliman  
(UPD), University of the Philippines Los Baños (UPLB), and University of San Carlos (USC).  
 
These universities collaborate to provide high -quality education and research opportunities in 
engineering and related fields. The ERDT scholarship program aims to support and develop highly 
qualified engineers and researchers who can contribute to the country's technological advancement 
and innovation.  
 
The main objective of the data study conducted on the Master of Science in Computer Applications 
program offered at MSU -Iligan Institute of Technology in Iligan City, Philippines was to assess 
its impact. Specifically, the study aimed to determine the strengths and weaknesses of the program 
in terms of its marketability, viability, financial stability, and social desirability. 
 
  
Checklist 29 

--- PAGE 116 ---
 
110 
 
 
As of the academic year 2022 -2023, the Master of Science in Computer Applications (MSCA) 
program at MSU -Iligan Institute of Technology, Iligan City, Philippines, has witn essed a 
consistent number of first -year admissions. Over the past six years, a total of forty (40) students 
have been admitted into the program, resulting in an average of approximately 7 students per year. 
 
This data indicates a significant value of the MSCA program in promoting high-quality education 
and research in the field of emerging technologies. The consistent number of first-year admissions 
demonstrates a steady interest and demand for the program among aspiring students who wish to 
specialize in computer applications. 
 
By enrolling an average of 7 students per year, the MSCA program has been able to provide 
focused attention and personalized instruction to each student. This small student -to-faculty ratio 
enhances the quality of education and ensures that students receive ample guidance and mentorship 
throughout their academic journey. 
 
Furthermore, the consistent enrollment figures signify the program's ability to attract and retain 
students over the years. This indicates that the MSCA program  is meeting the expectations and 
needs of students who seek advanced knowledge and skills in computer applications, preparing 
them for careers in the rapidly evolving technology industry. 
 
Moreover, the program's commitment to promoting research in emerging technologies is evident. 
Through the MSCA program, students have the opportunity to engage in cutting -edge research 
projects, contribute to the development of innovative solutions, and address real-world challenges 
in the field of computer applications. 
 
Overall, the data on first -year admissions and enrollment in the MSCA program highlight its 
significance in providing high-quality education, fostering research opportunities, and contributing 
to the advancement of emerging technologies. 


--- PAGE 117 ---
 
111 
 
 
 
 
To achieve these objectives, the study likely employed various research methodologies and data 
collection techniques. These may have included surveys, interviews with program stakeholders 
(such as faculty members, students, alumni, and employers), analysis of enrollment and graduation 
data, financial analysis of the program's budget and funding sources, and examination of the 
program's social relevance and impact within the local community and industry. 
 
By analyzing and evaluating these aspects, the study aimed to provide insights into the program's 
performance and effectiveness. The findings could be used to identify areas of improvement, 
enhance the program's market appeal, ensure its long-term financial sustainability, and align it with 
the needs and expectations of the stakeholders and the society at large. 
 
This data study employed the descriptive method utilizing questionnaires using online Google 
Forms. Checklist and documentary analysis were the main data gathering instruments. A 
screenshot of the form presented in a Google Form used in the survey.

The study conducted resulted as of June 2023 gathered data from a total of fourteen (14) 
respondents who participated in a Google Form survey. The data collected from the survey was 
presented in the form of graphs, providing insights into the participants' perspectives and 
preferences regarding the Master of Science in Computer Applications (MSCA) program. 
 
A. Do you intend to pursue Master of Science in Computer Applications (MSCA)?

- 43% Within the next two to three years , 36% August 2023, 21% N/A

Question A inquired about the respondents' intention to pursue the MSCA program. The survey 
revealed that 79% of the participants answered "Yes," indicating their interest  in pursuing the 
MSCA program, while 21% responded with "No." 
 
 
 
Question B aimed to determine when the respondents intended to pursue the MSCA program. The 
survey results showed that 43% of the participants planned to pursue the program within the next 
two to three years, 36% were considering starting in August 2023, and 21% did not specify a 
particular timeframe (N/A).

Question C delved into the reasons why the respondents wanted to enroll in the MSCA program.

the structured and specialized curriculum offered by the MSCA program.

Question D focused on the specific fi elds within Computer Applications that interested the 
respondents. The survey results revealed a range of interests among the participants. Some 
respondents (17%) were still undecided (N/A) about which field they wanted to specialize in. 
Among those who ha d a clear preference, 28% were interested in Embedded Systems, 11% in 
Programming/Firmware, 17% in Internet of Things (IoT), 5% in Database Management, 5% in 
Data Science and Analytics, 5% in Web Development, 6% in Active Directory, and 5% in 
Robotics. 
 
The presentation of this data through graphs provides a visual representation of the respondents' 
opinions and preferences. These findings offer valuable insights into the participants' motivations, 
timelines, and specific areas of interest within the MSCA program, aiding in the understanding of 
the target audience and informing program development and marketing strategies.

RTL COURSE SYLLABUS in MCA201 ADVANCED COMPUTER ORGANIZATION 
 
MSU-IIT 
Vision

 Course No./Title:  MCA201 ADVANCED COMPUTER ORGANIZATION 
Course Credit:  3 units 
Duration: 18 weeks (Semester Year: _______) 
Delivery Mode:  Asynchronous (remotely supervised) with a few synchronous sessions 
Level: Advanced 
Course Description: This is an introductory course on computer organization. It covers the different functional areas of a digital computer 
and discusses how these are interconnected, structured and organized: Basic computer logic: truth tables; logic 
equations, gates, combinatorial logic; basic computer arithmetic; binary numbers; addition and subtraction; floating 
point representation; system hierarchy; integrated circuit technology; performance; metrics; closing benchmarks; 
Amdahl’s law; instruction sets and operations; MIPS; assembly Language; machine language; examples of other 
instruction sets.  It covers topics in parallel computer architectures and RISC machines. 
Learning Culminating 
Outcome: 
By the end of this course, the student is able:  
1. To understand the concepts of computer organization 
2. To relate how the different components of the computer interact with each other.     
3. To learn the basic structure of modern / advanced digital computers 
Prerequisite: None 
Co-requisite: None 
Evaluation Criteria: Passing the course requires an overall percent of 60% 
Course 
Developers/Instructors: 
Prof. Joel I. Miano 
Department of Computer Applications  
joel.miano@g.msuiit.edu.ph / Consultation hours: 6:00-9:00 PM Weekdays

Classroom Polices: 
1. Observe excellent performance on the following: 
a) Honesty and Integrity; Punctuality/Attendance; Use class time appropriately; Remain in your seat until dismissed by your teacher. 
b) Use technology (i.e., Anycast, Bluetooth, WiFi, etc.) appropriately;  
c) Put cell phones and other noise makers on silent mode or turn them off. If you need to take a call, for some urgent or emergency reason, then please 
let the instructor know before class and then answer the call outside of the classroom. 
d) Follow obediently the computer laboratory policies implemented by the department. 
2. Respect the rights, opinions, ideas, and property of others: 
a) Be courteous.   
b) Raise hand before speaking.  
c) Perform class activities without interrupting/disturbing anyone.   
d) Use laboratory equipment properly to avoid accident, and ensure safety of others. 
3. Take active participation on class discussion, laboratory activities and department/college extracurricular activities 
4. Contribute to discussions by sharing new ideas, innovations and relevant researches 
5. Refrain/avoid inappropriate comments. 
6. Equality in the use of the laboratory facilities irrespective of gender. 
7. Observe 5S +1, (Sort, Set in order, Shine, Standardize, Sustain, and Safety). 
8. Stewards of environment thru the conduct of research related activities that protects the environment 
9. Involvement in the promotion on Green Technology 
 
References: 
 
1. Linda Null, Julia Lobur. The essentials of computer organization and architecture, 5th edition, 2021  
2. Computer System Architecture: By M. Morris Mano, 3rd edition 
3. Andrew S. Tanenbaum, Structured Computer Organization, Prentice Hall Intonation Editions, 6th edition, 2013 
4. Hamacker, Vranesaic and Zaky, Computer Organization and Architecture, 2002 
5. John P. Hayes, Computer Architecture and Organization, 1991

RTL COURSE SYLLABUS in MCA202 ADVANCED OPERATING SYSTEMS 
 
MSU-IIT 
Vision 
A research university committed to the 
holistic development of the individual 
and society. 
 
Mission 
To provide quality education for the 
sustainable development of the nation 
and the global community. 
 
COLLEGE OF COMPUTER 
STUDIES 
Vision 
A Center of Excellence in Information 
and Communication Technology 
manned by motivated and highly 
competent workforce who adheres to 
Institute policies; equipped with state- 
of-the-art infrastructure; founded on 
relevant instruction, strong culture of 
Research & Extension and enhanced 
resource-generating programs 
producing highly competitive 
graduates imbued with professional 
values. 
 
Mission 
Transform the deserving sector of the 
society into highly competitive 
graduates who will respond to the 
needs of the Local and International 
industries for ICT professionals. 
 Course No./Title:  MCA202 ADVANCED OPERATING SYSTEMS 
Course Credit:  3 units 
Duration: 18 weeks (Semester Year: _______) 
Delivery Mode:  Asynchronous (remotely supervised) with a few synchronous sessions 
Level: Advanced 
Course Description: The study of a broad range of behaviors arising from complex system design, including low-level operating 
systems, resource sharing and scheduling, interactions between hardware and software, network-protocol 
design and implementation, separation of mutually distrusting parties on a common platform, and control 
of distributed-system behaviors such as concurrency and data replication. 
Learning Culminating 
Outcome: 
By the end of this course, the student is able:  
1. To understand and describe the high-level OS kernel structure. 
2. To gained insight into hardware-software interactions for compute and I/O. 
3. To exposed to research ideas in system structure and behavior. 
4. To learn how to write systems-style performance evaluations. 
Prerequisite: None 
Co-requisite: None 
Evaluation Criteria: Passing the course requires an overall percent of 60% 
Course 
Developers/Instructors: 
Prof. Joel I. Miano 
Department of Computer Applications  
joel.miano@g.msuiit.edu.ph / Consultation hours: 6:00-9:00 PM Weekdays

Classroom Polices: 
1. Observe excellent performance on the following: 
a) Honesty and Integrity; Punctuality/Attendance; Use class time appropriately; Remain in your seat until dismissed by your teacher. 
b) Use technology (i.e., Anycast, Bluetooth, WiFi, etc.) appropriately;

RTL COURSE SYLLABUS in MCA203 SYSTEMS DEVELOPMENT WITH EMERGING TECHNOLOGIES 
 
MSU-IIT 
Vision 
A research university committed to the 
holistic development of the individual 
and society. 
 
Mission 
To provide quality education for the 
sustainable development of the nation 
and the global community. 
 
COLLEGE OF COMPUTER 
STUDIES 
Vision 
A Center of Excellence in Information 
and Communication Technology 
manned by motivated and highly 
competent workforce who adheres to 
Institute policies; equipped with state- 
of-the-art infrastructure; founded on 
relevant instruction, strong culture of 
Research & Extension and enhanced 
resource-generating programs 
producing highly competitive 
graduates imbued with professional 
values. 
 
Mission 
Transform the deserving sector of the 
society into highly competitive 
graduates who will respond to the 
needs of the Local and International 
industries for ICT professionals. 
 Course No./Title:  MCA203 SYSTEMS DEVELOPMENT WITH EMERGING TECHNOLOGIES 
Course Credit:  3 units 
Duration: 18 weeks (Semester Year: _______) 
Delivery Mode:  Asynchronous (remotely supervised) with a few synchronous sessions 
Level: Advanced 
Course Description: This course focuses on the development of software application using the web, mobile and emerging 
technologies. Emphasis is on the requirements management, interface design, usability, and deployment 
including ethical and legal considerations. Topics include file-handling, front-end development with create-
retrieve-update-delete (CRUD) modules, event-driven programming, and data manipulation. 
Learning Culminating 
Outcome: 
By the end of this course, the student is able:  
1. To produce graduates who are capable to conduct research and development and produce patentable innovations. 
2. To be able to cater to the demands of Information and Communication Technology (ICT) in helping to solve the 
emerging and future global problems. 
3. To align the program with the requirements set by national and international standards such as CHED PSG and 
Seoul Accord. 
4. To produce graduates as prospective enrollees for the Master of Science in Computer Applications (MSCA), offered 
in the School of Computer Studies, thereby supporting the role of MSU-IIT as the only delivering institution for 
engineering Research and Development for Technology (ERDT) consortium and CHED. 
Prerequisite: None 
Co-requisite: None 
Evaluation Criteria: Passing the course requires an overall percent of 60% 
Course 
Developers/Instructors: 
Prof. Maria Fe P. Bahinting 
Department of Computer Applications  
mariafe.bahinting@g.msuiit.edu.ph / Consultation hours: 6:00-9:00 PM Weekdays

II. Course Outcomes: 
At the end of the term, students would be able to: 
1. Develop specifications for a software development effort that precisely articulates the functional requirements, expected execution 
paths and the explicit use of the cutting edge or emerging technologies which includes hardware devices and software library APIs. 
2. Select and use a defined coding, documentation writing and licensing standards in a sufficiently complex software project where 
coding idioms and mechanism for implementing designs to achieve desired properties such as reliability, efficiency and robustness 
are practiced with respect to legal and ethical considerations. 
3. Undertake, as part of a team activity, an inspection of the source code and unit testing of the functional units of a sufficiently complex 
software project.

RTL COURSE SYLLABUS in MCA221 ADVANCED EMBEDDED SYSTEMS 
 
MSU-IIT 
Vision 
A research university committed to the 
holistic development of the individual 
and society. 
 
Mission 
To provide quality education for the 
sustainable development of the nation 
and the global community. 
 
COLLEGE OF COMPUTER 
STUDIES 
Vision 
A Center of Excellence in Information 
and Communication Technology 
manned by motivated and highly 
competent workforce who adheres to 
Institute policies; equipped with state- 
of-the-art infrastructure; founded on 
relevant instruction, strong culture of 
Research & Extension and enhanced 
resource-generating programs 
producing highly competitive 
graduates imbued with professional 
values. 
 
Mission 
Transform the deserving sector of the 
society into highly competitive 
graduates who will respond to the 
needs of the Local and International 
industries for ICT professionals. 
 Course No./Title:  MCA221 ADVANCED EMBEDDED SYSTEMS 
Course Credit:  3 units 
Duration: 18 weeks (Semester Year: _______) 
Delivery Mode:  Asynchronous (remotely supervised) with a few synchronous sessions 
Level: Advanced 
Course Description: This course will introduce advanced topics in the principles of embedded system, measurement system 
design in Analog to Digital Converters and Sensors used in interfacing, ARM processor fundamentals, 
design of FPGA-based embedded systems using VHDL Fundamentals subprogram and files - including 
data stream management, embedded s ystems for multi -media, real -time embedded systems, and 
embedded system security. 
Learning Culminating 
Outcome: 
By the end of this course, the student is able:  
1. To understand and describe the principles of embedded system 
2. To apply measurement system design in Analog to Digital Converters and Sensors used in interfacing. 
3. To program, design, analyze and implement FPGA-based embedded systems using VHDL Fundamentals 
subprogram and files. 
4. To apply the design, analyze and implement about ARM fundamentals writing codes. 
Prerequisite: None 
Co-requisite: None 
Evaluation Criteria: Passing the course requires an overall percent of 60% 
Course 
Developers/Instructors: 
Prof. Joel I. Miano 
Department of Computer Applications  
joel.miano@g.msuiit.edu.ph / Consultation hours: 6:00-9:00 PM Weekdays

CCS Commitment 
Integral to the attainment of its 
mission, the College commits itself 
to: 
1. Develop a highly motivated 
versatile ICT workforce. 
2. Offer highly specialized and 
ladderized programs. 
3. Keep abreast with state-of-the-art 
technology. 
4. Develop a strong culture of 
research, extension and production. 
 
CA DEPARTMENT 
 
1.To understand the design & 
development of hardware device and 
software programs through specialized 
skills in Embedded System and Internet 
of Things (IoT). 
 
2.To sharpen the mathematical analysis 
and produce patentable innovations to 
cater the demands of Information and 
Communication Technology (ICT) in 
helping to solve the emerging and 
future global problems. 
 Outcomes for HIGHER 
EDUCATION INSTITUTION:  
Outcomes common to the Master of Science in 
Computer Applications: 
 
Outcome as a State 
University as stipulated in 
CMO 46 s 2012: 
A. To keep abreast of latest 
developments in the specific 
field of practice; 
B. Effectively communicate using 
English and Filipino, orally and 
in writing; 
C. Work effectively and 
independently in multi-
disciplinary and multi-cultural 
teams; 
D. Exemplify professional, social, 
ethical, and environmental 
responsibility; 
E. Preserve and promote “Filipino 
historical and cultural heritage” 
(based on RA 7722); and 
F. Advocate for peace in multi-
cultural settings. 
G. Apply knowledge of mathematics and sciences to 
solve computer electronics problems. 
H. Analyze a problem, formulate and identify solutions 
for computer applications and technology   problems 
using analytical tools appropriate to areas of 
specialization. 
I. Apply design principle using software and firmware for 
broadly defined computer applications. 
J. Implement and evaluate computer application 
systems, components or processes to meet specific 
needs. 
K. Select and apply appropriate techniques, resources 
and modern computing and ICT tools necessary for 
computer applications practices. 
L. Function effectively as a member or leader of a 
development team recognizing the different roles 
within a team to accomplish a common goal. 
M. Communicate effectively with the computer 
applications community and with society at large 
about complex computer application activities through 
logical writing, presentations, and clear instructions. 
N. Understand and commit to professional ethics and 
responsibilities and norms of computer and cyber 
technology practices. 
O. Recognize the need for and have the ability, to 
engage in independent learning for continual 
development as a technology specialist. 
P. Ability to generate new 
knowledge in the form of 
research or developmental 
projects to support national, 
regional, or local 
development plans

Classroom Polices: 
1. Observe excellent performance on the following: 
a) Honesty and Integrity; Punctuality/Attendance; Use class time appropriately; Remain in your seat until dismissed by your teacher. 
b) Use technology (i.e., Anycast, Bluetooth, WiFi, etc.) appropriately;  
c) Put cell phones and other noise makers on silent mode or turn them off. If you need to take a call, for some urgent or emergency reason, then please 
let the instructor know before class and then answer the call outside of the classroom. 
d) Follow obediently the computer laboratory policies implemented by the department. 
2. Respect the rights, opinions, ideas, and property of others: 
a) Be courteous.   
b) Raise hand before speaking.  
c) Perform class activities without interrupting/disturbing anyone.   
d) Use laboratory equipment properly to avoid accident, and ensure safety of others. 
3. Take active participation on class discussion, laboratory activities and department/college extracurricular activities 
4. Contribute to discussions by sharing new ideas, innovations and relevant researches 
5. Refrain/avoid inappropriate comments. 
6. Equality in the use of the laboratory facilities irrespective of gender. 
7. Observe 5S +1, (Sort, Set in order, Shine, Standardize, Sustain, and Safety). 
8. Stewards of environment thru the conduct of research related activities that protects the environment 
9. Involvement in the promotion on Green Technology 
 
References: 
 
1. Stuart R. Ball, Analog Interfacing to Embedded Microprocessor Systems, 2001. 
2. John G. Webster , The measurement, Instrumentation & sensors,Handbook,1999. 
3. Dogan Ibrahim, Microcontroller-Based Temperature Monitoring and Control, Newnes, 2nd Edition ,2002. 
4. Peter J.Ashenden, “The Designer’s guide to VHDL”,3rd Edition, May 2008. 
5. Charles H. Roth, Jr.  “Digital System Design using VHDL", Thomson Learning Inc., 2008 
6. Douglas Perry, “VHDL Programming by Example”, Tata McGraw Hill, 4th Edition 2002 ACC.NO: B101456 
7. Skahill. K, “VHDL for Programmable Logic”, 1996

A Center of Excellence in Information 
and Communication Technology 
manned by motivated and highly 
competent workforce who adheres to 
Institute policies; equipped with state- 
of-the-art infrastructure; founded on 
relevant instruction, strong culture of 
Research & Extension and enhanced 
resource-generating programs 
producing highly competitive 
graduates imbued with professional 
values. 
 
Mission 
Transform the deserving sector of the 
society into highly competitive 
graduates who will respond to the 
needs of the Local and International 
industries for ICT professionals. 
 Course No./Title:  MCA222 ADVANCE DIGITAL SIGNAL PROCESSING 
Course Credit:  3 units 
Duration: 18 weeks (Semester Year: _______) 
Delivery Mode:  Asynchronous (remotely supervised) with a few synchronous sessions 
Level: Advanced 
Course Description: This course will introduce students to explore sampled signals and digital processing, random signals, 
representing signals and systems, temporal and spatial signal processing, frequency analysis of signals 
and discrete-time filters and recursive filters. A conversion of the real-world signals to digital form and then 
conversion back to the analog form following the processing. These include the conversion from analog 
to digital and vice versa, digital filtering, transforms, noise and its implications, estimation and prediction.  
Learning Culminating 
Outcome: 
By the end of this course, the student is able:  
1. To understand and describe the sampling theorem. 
2. To Determine the frequency response and transfer function of FIR and IIR filter.  
3. To program, design, analyze and implement analog filter design in Matlab.  
4. To apply the design, analyze and implement Artificial Neural Network (ANN) design in Matlab. 
Prerequisite: None 
Co-requisite: None 
Evaluation Criteria: Passing the course requires an overall percent of 60% 
Course 
Developers/Instructors: 
Prof. Joel I. Miano 
Department of Computer Applications  
joel.miano@g.msuiit.edu.ph / Consultation hours: 6:00-9:00 PM Weekdays

Classroom Polices: 
1. Observe excellent performance on the following: 
a) Honesty and Integrity; Punctuality/Attendance; Use class time appropriately; Remain in your seat until dismissed by your teacher. 
b) Use technology (i.e., Anycast, Bluetooth, WiFi, etc.) appropriately;  
c) Put cell phones and other noise makers on silent mode or turn them off. If you need to take a call, for some urgent or emergency reason, then please 
let the instructor know before class and then answer the call outside of the classroom. 
d) Follow obediently the computer laboratory policies implemented by the department. 
2. Respect the rights, opinions, ideas, and property of others: 
a) Be courteous.   
b) Raise hand before speaking.  
c) Perform class activities without interrupting/disturbing anyone.   
d) Use laboratory equipment properly to avoid accident, and ensure safety of others. 
3. Take active participation on class discussion, laboratory activities and department/college extracurricular activities 
4. Contribute to discussions by sharing new ideas, innovations and relevant researches 
5. Refrain/avoid inappropriate comments. 
6. Equality in the use of the laboratory facilities irrespective of gender.

RTL COURSE SYLLABUS in MCA223 ADVANCED COMPUTER VISION 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
MSU-IIT 
Vision 
A research university committed to the 
holistic development of the individual 
and society. 
 
Mission 
To provide quality education for the 
sustainable development of the nation 
and the global community. 
 
COLLEGE OF COMPUTER 
STUDIES 
Vision 
A Center of Excellence in Information 
and Communication Technology 
manned by motivated and highly 
competent workforce who adheres to 
Institute policies; equipped with state- 
of-the-art infrastructure; founded on 
relevant instruction, strong culture of 
Research & Extension and enhanced 
resource-generating programs 
producing highly competitive 
graduates imbued with professional 
values. 
 
Mission 
Transform the deserving sector of the 
society into highly competitive 
graduates who will respond to the 
needs of the Local and International 
industries for ICT professionals. 
 Course No./Title:  MCA223 ADVANCED COMPUTER VISION 
Course Credit:  3 units 
Duration: 18 weeks (Semester Year: _______) 
Delivery Mode:  Asynchronous (remotely supervised) with a few synchronous sessions 
Level: Advanced 
Course Description: This course introduces the fundamentals of computer vision. It will focus on fundamental models and algorithms in 
computer vision, including such topics as image formation, image sensing, image filtering, edge extraction, tracking 
and machine learning. The course will also provide an overview of the challenges of vision, the common approaches 
and current techniques. 
Learning Culminating 
Outcome: 
By the end of this course, the student is able:  
1. To familiar with both the theoretical and practical aspects of computing with images, described the foundation 
of image formation, measurement, and analysis; 
2. To focus implemention of common methods for robust image matching and alignment and understand the 
geometric relationships between 2D images and the 3D world; 
3. Have gained exposure to object and scene recognition and categorization from images, principles of state-of-
the-art deep neural networks; and 
4. Developed the practical skills necessary to build computer vision applications. The student is able to apply the 
design, analyze and implement Artificial Neural Network (ANN) design in Matlab. 
Prerequisite: None 
Co-requisite: None 
Evaluation Criteria: Passing the course requires an overall percent of 60% 
Course 
Developers/Instructors: 
Engr. Maria Fe P. Bahinting         
Department of Computer Applications  
mariafe.bahinting@g.msuiit.edu.ph

Classroom Polices: 
1. Observe excellent performance on the following: 
a) Honesty and Integrity; Punctuality/Attendance; Use class time appropriately; Remain in your seat until dismissed by your teacher. 
b) Use technology (i.e., Anycast, Bluetooth, WiFi, etc.) appropriately;  
c) Put cell phones and other noise makers on silent mode or turn them off. If you need to take a call, for some urgent or emergency reason, then please 
let the instructor know before class and then answer the call outside of the classroom. 
d) Follow obediently the computer laboratory policies implemented by the department. 
2. Respect the rights, opinions, ideas, and property of others: 
a) Be courteous.   
b) Raise hand before speaking.  
c) Perform class activities without interrupting/disturbing anyone.   
d) Use laboratory equipment properly to avoid accident, and ensure safety of others. 
3. Take active participation on class discussion, laboratory activities and department/college extracurricular activities 
4. Contribute to discussions by sharing new ideas, innovations and relevant researches 
5. Refrain/avoid inappropriate comments. 
6. Equality in the use of the laboratory facilities irrespective of gender. 
7. Observe 5S +1, (Sort, Set in order, Shine, Standardize, Sustain, and Safety). 
8. Stewards of environment thru the conduct of research related activities that protects the environment 
9. Involvement in the promotion on Green Technology

RTL COURSE SYLLABUS in MCA224 APPLIED MACHINE LEARNING FOR EMBEDDED SYSTEMS 
 
MSU-IIT 
Vision 
A research university committed to the 
holistic development of the individual 
and society. 
 
Mission 
To provide quality education for the 
sustainable development of the nation 
and the global community. 
 
COLLEGE OF COMPUTER 
STUDIES 
Vision 
A Center of Excellence in Information 
and Communication Technology 
manned by motivated and highly 
competent workforce who adheres to 
Institute policies; equipped with state- 
of-the-art infrastructure; founded on 
relevant instruction, strong culture of 
Research & Extension and enhanced 
resource-generating programs 
producing highly competitive 
graduates imbued with professional 
values. 
 
Mission 
Transform the deserving sector of the 
society into highly competitive 
graduates who will respond to the 
needs of the Local and International 
industries for ICT professionals. 
 Course No./Title:  MCA224 APPLIED MACHINE LEARNING FOR EMBEDDED SYSTEMS 
Course Credit:  3 units 
Duration: 18 weeks (Semester Year: _______) 
Delivery Mode:  Asynchronous (remotely supervised) with a few synchronous sessions 
Level: Advanced 
Course Description: This course will introduce students on applying machine learning in embedded systems to simplify 
development of useful machine -learning applications, which covers Machine -learning methods, 
Supervised learning, Neural network development, Data preparation, Model development, neural network 
frameworks development methods, discuses platform requirements, and covers specialized frameworks 
and architectures. 
Learning Culminating 
Outcome: 
By the end of this course, the student is able:  
1. To understand and describe the Machine-learning methods and Supervised learning. 
2. To determine the neural network development, data preparation and Model development.  
3. To program, design, analyze and implement neural network frameworks development methods 
and platform requirements. 
4. To apply the design, analyze and implement specialized frameworks and architectures. 
Prerequisite: None 
Co-requisite: None 
Evaluation Criteria: Passing the course requires an overall percent of 60% 
Course 
Developers/Instructors: 
Prof. Joel I. Miano 
Department of Computer Applications  
joel.miano@g.msuiit.edu.ph / Consultation hours: 6:00-9:00 PM Weekdays

Classroom Polices: 
1. Observe excellent performance on the following: 
a) Honesty and Integrity; Punctuality/Attendance; Use class time appropriately; Remain in your seat until dismissed by your teacher. 
b) Use technology (i.e., Anycast, Bluetooth, WiFi, etc.) appropriately;  
c) Put cell phones and other noise makers on silent mode or turn them off. If you need to take a call, for some urgent or emergency reason, then please 
let the instructor know before class and then answer the call outside of the classroom.

RTL COURSE SYLLABUS in MCA225 ADVANCED INTERNET OF THINGS (IoT) 
 
MSU-IIT 
Vision 
A research university committed to the 
holistic development of the individual 
and society. 
 
Mission 
To provide quality education for the 
sustainable development of the nation 
and the global community. 
 
COLLEGE OF COMPUTER 
STUDIES 
Vision 
A Center of Excellence in Information 
and Communication Technology 
manned by motivated and highly 
competent workforce who adheres to 
Institute policies; equipped with state- 
of-the-art infrastructure; founded on 
relevant instruction, strong culture of 
Research & Extension and enhanced 
resource-generating programs 
producing highly competitive 
graduates imbued with professional 
values. 
 
Mission 
Transform the deserving sector of the 
society into highly competitive 
graduates who will respond to the 
needs of the Local and International 
industries for ICT professionals. 
 Course No./Title:  MCA225 ADVANCED INTERNET OF THINGS (IoT) 
Course Credit:  3 units ( 2 hours lecture, 3 hours laboratory) 
Duration: 18 weeks 
Delivery Mode:  Asynchronous (remotely supervised) with a few synchronous sessions 
Level: Advanced 
Course Description: This course focuses on identifying, designing, prototyping, and presenting an IoT solution that securely 
solves a current business or social problem. It also explores the field of the things and their connection to 
the IoT. 
Learning Culminating 
Outcome: 
1.To produce graduates who are capable to conduct research and development and produce patentable innovations. 
2.To be able to cater to the demands of Information and Communication Technology (ICT) in helping to solve the 
emerging and future global problems. 
3.To align the program with the requirements set by national and international standards such as  CHED PSG and 
Seoul Accord. 
 4.To produce graduates as prospective enrollees for the Master of Science in Computer Applications (MSCA), 
offered in the School of Computer Studies, thereby supporting the role of MSU-IIT as the only delivering institution for 
engineering Research and Development for Technology (ERDT) consortium and CHED. 
Prerequisite: None 
Co-requisite: None 
Course 
Developers/Instructors: 
Assoc. Prof. Alexander R Gaw 
alexander.gaw@g.msuiit.edu.ph

CA DEPARTMENT 
 
1.To understand the design &

of Things (IoT).

field of practice;

solve computer electronics problems.

for computer applications and technology   problems 
using analytical tools appropriate to areas of 
specialization. 
I. Apply design principle using software and firmware for 
broadly defined computer applications. 
J. Implement and evaluate computer application 
systems, components or processes to meet specific 
needs. 
K. Select and apply appropriate techniques, resources 
and modern computing and ICT tools necessary for 
computer applications practices. 
L. Function effectively as a member or leader of a 
development team recognizing the different roles 
within a team to accomplish a common goal. 
M. Communicate effectively with the computer 
applications community and with society at large 
about complex computer application activities through 
logical writing, presentations, and clear instructions. 
N. Understand and commit to professional ethics and 
responsibilities and norms of computer and cyber 
technology practices. 
O. Recognize the need for and have the ability, to 
engage in independent learning for continual 
development as a technology specialist. 
P. Ability to generate new 
knowledge in the form of 
research or developmental 
projects to support national, 
regional, or local 
development plans

Classroom Polices: 
1. Observe excellent performance on the following: 
a) Honesty and Integrity; Punctuality/Attendance; Use class time appropriately; Remain in your seat until dismissed by your teacher. 
b) Use technology (i.e., Anycast, Bluetooth, WiFi, etc.) appropriately;  
c) Put cell phones and other noise makers on silent mode or turn them off. If you need to take a call, for some urgent or emergency reason, then please 
let the instructor know before class and then answer the call outside of the classroom. 
d) Follow obediently the computer laboratory policies implemented by the department. 
2. Respect the rights, opinions, ideas, and property of others: 
a) Be courteous.   
b) Raise hand before speaking.  
c) Perform class activities without interrupting/disturbing anyone.   
d) Use laboratory equipment properly to avoid accident, and ensure safety of others. 
3. Take active participation on class discussion, laboratory activities and department/college extracurricular activities 
4. Contribute to discussions by sharing new ideas, innovations and relevant researches 
5. Refrain/avoid inappropriate comments. 
6. Equality in the use of the laboratory facilities irrespective of gender. 
7. Observe 5S +1, (Sort, Set in order, Shine, Standardize, Sustain, and Safety). 
8. Stewards of environment thru the conduct of research related activities that protects the environment 
9. Involvement in the promotion on Green Technology 
 
References: 
 
1. Monk, S. (2015). Programming the Raspberry Pi. McGraw-Hill Education TAB; 2nd edition 
2. Pfister, C. (2011). Getting Started with the Internet of Things(1st ed). Make Community, LLC; 1st edition (June 21, 2011) 
3. Robinson, A.(2013). Raspberry Pi Projects. Wiley; 1st edition 
4. Gay, W. (2018). Advanced Raspberry Pi: Raspbian Linux and GPIO Integration. Apress; 2nd ed. edition

RTL COURSE SYLLABUS in MCA 227 ADVANCED CLOUD COMPUTING  
 
MSU-IIT 
Vision 
A research university committed to the 
holistic development of the individual 
and society. 
 
Mission 
To provide quality education for the 
sustainable development of the nation 
and the global community. 
 
COLLEGE OF COMPUTER 
STUDIES 
Vision 
A Center of Excellence in Information 
and Communication Technology 
manned by motivated and highly 
competent workforce who adheres to 
Institute policies; equipped with state- 
of-the-art infrastructure; founded on 
relevant instruction, strong culture of 
Research & Extension and enhanced 
resource-generating programs 
producing highly competitive 
graduates imbued with professional 
values. 
 
Mission 
Transform the deserving sector of the 
society into highly competitive 
graduates who will respond to the 
needs of the Local and International 
industries for ICT professionals. 
 Course No./Title: MCA226 NETWORK SECURITY FOR INTERNET OF THINGS (IoT) 
Course Credit: 3 units (2 hours lecture, 3 hours laboratory) 
Duration: 18 weeks 
Delivery Mode: Hybrid  
Level: Advanced 
Course Description:   This course focus in providing student with knowledge, skills, and awareness of the challenge of IoT 
security and the process of evaluating security risk in IoT systems.  
Program Educational 
Objectives 
1.To produce graduates who are capable to conduct research and development and produce 
patentable innovations. 
2.To be able to cater to the demands of Information and Communication Technology (ICT) in 
helping to solve the emerging and future global problems. 
3.To align the program with the requirements set by national and international standards such 
as  CHED PSG and Seoul Accord. 
 4.To produce graduates as prospective enrollees for the Master of Science in Computer 
Applications (MSCA), offered in the School of Computer Studies, thereby supporting the role of 
MSU-IIT as the only delivering institution for engineering Research and Development for 
Technology (ERDT) consortium and CHED. 
Prerequisite: None 
Co-requisite: None 
Course 
Developers/Instructors: 
Assoc. Prof. Alexander R Gaw 
alexander.gaw@g.msuiit.edu.ph

CA DEPARTMENT 
 
1.To understand the design & 
development of hardware device and 
software programs through specialized 
skills in Embedded System and Internet 
of Things (IoT). 
 
2.To sharpen the mathematical analysis 
and produce patentable innovations to 
cater the demands of Information and 
Communication Technology (ICT) in 
helping to solve the emerging and 
future global problems. 
 Outcomes for HIGHER 
EDUCATION INSTITUTION:  
Outcomes common to the Master of Science in 
Computer Applications: 
 
Outcome as a State 
University as stipulated in 
CMO 46 s 2012: 
A. To keep abreast of latest 
developments in the specific 
field of practice; 
B. Effectively communicate using 
English and Filipino, orally and 
in writing; 
C. Work effectively and 
independently in multi-
disciplinary and multi-cultural 
teams;

ethical, and environmental 
responsibility; 
E. Preserve and promote “Filipino 
historical and cultural heritage” 
(based on RA 7722); and 
F. Advocate for peace in multi-
cultural settings. 
G. Apply knowledge of mathematics and sciences to 
solve computer electronics problems. 
H. Analyze a problem, formulate and identify solutions 
for computer applications and technology   problems 
using analytical tools appropriate to areas of 
specialization. 
I. Apply design principle using software and firmware for 
broadly defined computer applications. 
J. Implement and evaluate computer application 
systems, components or processes to meet specific 
needs. 
K. Select and apply appropriate techniques, resources 
and modern computing and ICT tools necessary for 
computer applications practices. 
L. Function effectively as a member or leader of a 
development team recognizing the different roles 
within a team to accomplish a common goal. 
M. Communicate effectively with the computer 
applications community and with society at large 
about complex computer application activities through 
logical writing, presentations, and clear instructions. 
N. Understand and commit to professional ethics and 
responsibilities and norms of computer and cyber 
technology practices. 
O. Recognize the need for and have the ability, to 
engage in independent learning for continual 
development as a technology specialist. 
P. Ability to generate new 
knowledge in the form of 
research or developmental 
projects to support national, 
regional, or local 
development plans

Publishing. ISBN 13: 
9781787280571

RTL COURSE SYLLABUS in MCA227 ADVANCED CLOUD COMPUTING  
MSU-IIT 
Vision 
A research university committed to the 
holistic development of the individual 
and society. 
 
Mission 
To provide quality education for the 
sustainable development of the nation 
and the global community. 
 
COLLEGE OF COMPUTER 
STUDIES 
Vision 
A Center of Excellence in Information 
and Communication Technology 
manned by motivated and highly 
competent workforce who adheres to 
Institute policies; equipped with state- 
of-the-art infrastructure; founded on 
relevant instruction, strong culture of 
Research & Extension and enhanced 
resource-generating programs 
producing highly competitive 
graduates imbued with professional 
values. 
 
Mission 
Transform the deserving sector of the 
society into highly competitive 
graduates who will respond to the 
needs of the Local and International 
industries for ICT professionals. 
 Course No./Title: MCA227 ADVANCED CLOUD COMPUTING  
Course Credit: 3 units (2 hours lecture, 3 hours laboratory) 
Duration: 18 weeks 
Delivery Mode: Hybrid  
Level: Advanced 
Course Description: This course provides a theoretical and conceptual knowledge and overview of essential to the understanding 
of cloud computing. It also covers various service level security issues and several open challenges for 
adoption and its future implications. Further, this course provides a hands -on, programming -oriented 
introduction to cloud computing with Amazon Web Services (AWS). Students will learn how to use AWS 
services such as S3, EC2, Lambda, and ECS to create apps. 
Program Educational 
Objectives 
1.To produce graduates who are capable to conduct research and development and produce patentable 
innovations. 
2.To be able to cater to the demands of Information and Communication Technology (ICT) in helping to 
solve the emerging and future global problems. 
3.To align the program with the requirements set by national and international standards such as  CHED 
PSG and Seoul Accord. 
 4.To produce graduates as prospective enrollees for the Master of Science in Computer Applications 
(MSCA), offered in the School of Computer Studies, thereby supporting the role of MSU -IIT as the only 
delivering institution for engineering Research and Development for Technology (ERDT) consortium and 
CHED. 
Prerequisite: None 
Co-requisite: None 
Course 
Developers/Instructors: 
Prof. Maria Fe P. Bahinting 
mariafe.bahinting@g.msuiit.edu.ph / Consultation hours: 6:00-9:00 PM Weekdays

Classroom Polices: 
1. Observe excellent performance on the following: 
a) Honesty and Integrity; Punctuality/Attendance; Use class time appropriately; Remain in your seat until dismissed by your teacher. 
b) Use technology (i.e., Anycast, Bluetooth, WiFi, etc.) appropriately;  
c) Put cell phones and other noise makers on silent mode or turn them off. If you need to take a call, for some urgent or emergency reason, then please 
let the instructor know before class and then answer the call outside of the classroom. 
d) Follow obediently the computer laboratory policies implemented by the department. 
2. Respect the rights, opinions, ideas, and property of others: 
a) Be courteous.   
b) Raise hand before speaking.  
c) Perform class activities without interrupting/disturbing anyone.   
d) Use laboratory equipment properly to avoid accident, and ensure safety of others. 
3. Take active participation on class discussion, laboratory activities and department/college extracurricular activities 
4. Contribute to discussions by sharing new ideas, innovations and relevant researches 
5. Refrain/avoid inappropriate comments. 
6. Equality in the use of the laboratory facilities irrespective of gender. 
7. Observe 5S +1, (Sort, Set in order, Shine, Standardize, Sustain, and Safety). 
8. Stewards of environment thru the conduct of research related activities that protects the environment 
9. Involvement in the promotion on Green Technology 
 
References: 
 
1. Artificial Neural Networks in Real-Life Applications, by Juan Ramon Rabunal, Julian Dorrado  
2. Neural networks in business: techniques and application, by Kate Smith & Jatinder Gupta (2002), Online: https://1lib.ph/book/683594/bb58cc / 
https://www.pdfdrive.com/neuralnetworks-a-comprehensivefoundationpdf-d18774300.html 
3. Neural Network Systems Techniques and Applications. Vol 2, Optimization Tecjniques, Cornelios T. Leonides (1998) Online: 
https://1lib.ph/book/3154012/1e4f47

RTL COURSE SYLLABUS in MCA228 APPLIED BIG DATA AND ANALYTICS FOR IOT  
MSU-IIT 
Vision 
A research university committed to the 
holistic development of the individual 
and society. 
 
Mission 
To provide quality education for the 
sustainable development of the nation 
and the global community. 
 
COLLEGE OF COMPUTER 
STUDIES 
Vision 
A Center of Excellence in Information 
and Communication Technology 
manned by motivated and highly 
competent workforce who adheres to 
Institute policies; equipped with state- 
of-the-art infrastructure; founded on 
relevant instruction, strong culture of 
Research & Extension and enhanced 
resource-generating programs 
producing highly competitive 
graduates imbued with professional 
values. 
 
Mission 
Transform the deserving sector of the 
society into highly competitive 
graduates who will respond to the 
needs of the Local and International 
industries for ICT professionals. 
 Course No./Title: MCA228 APPLIED BIG DATA AND ANALYTICS FOR IOT  
Course Credit: 3 units (2 hours lecture, 3 hours laboratory) 
Duration: 18 weeks 
Delivery Mode: Hybrid  
Level: Advanced 
Course Description: The Internet of Things is the emphasis of this course, which covers data and analytic flows. Students will also learn 
about data security, device identity, enormous data volumes, and real -time processing as they learn about big data 
analytics. The course also looks at the issues with collecting data from IoT devices  and transferring it to the cloud, as 
well as current designs. Students will also learn how to use Apache Spark, Storm, and Kafka to construct a messaging 
and data streaming system using a hands-on approach in Amazon Web Services (AWS) with simulated data. They will 
also learn how to use the Hadoop environment to execute real -time pattern analysis with IoT data and gain better 
predictive insights in order to create actionable triggers for business and data mining applications. 
Program Educational 
Objectives 
1.To produce graduates who are capable to conduct research and development and produce patentable innovations. 
2.To be able to cater to the demands of Information and Communication Technology (ICT) in helping to solve the 
emerging and future global problems. 
3.To align the program with the requirements set by national and international standards such as  CHED PSG and 
Seoul Accord. 
 4.To produce graduates as prospective enrollees for the Master of Science in Computer Applications (MSCA), 
offered in the School of Computer Studies, thereby supporting the role of MSU-IIT as the only delivering institution for 
engineering Research and Development for Technology (ERDT) consortium and CHED. 
Prerequisite: None 
Co-requisite: None 
Course 
Developers/Instructors: 
Engr. Maria Fe P. Bahinting 
mariafe.bahinting@g.msuiit.edu.ph / Consultation hours: 6:00-9:00 PM Weekdays

Classroom Polices: 
1. Observe excellent performance on the following: 
a) Honesty and Integrity; Punctuality/Attendance; Use class time appropriately; Remain in your seat until dismissed by your teacher. 
b) Use technology (i.e., Anycast, Bluetooth, WiFi, etc.) appropriately;  
c) Put cell phones and other noise makers on silent mode or turn them off. If you need to take a call, for some urgent or emergency reason, then please 
let the instructor know before class and then answer the call outside of the classroom. 
d) Follow obediently the computer laboratory policies implemented by the department. 
2. Respect the rights, opinions, ideas, and property of others: 
a) Be courteous.   
b) Raise hand before speaking.  
c) Perform class activities without interrupting/disturbing anyone.   
d) Use laboratory equipment properly to avoid accident, and ensure safety of others. 
3. Take active participation on class discussion, laboratory activities and department/college extracurricular activities 
4. Contribute to discussions by sharing new ideas, innovations and relevant researches 
5. Refrain/avoid inappropriate comments. 
6. Equality in the use of the laboratory facilities irrespective of gender. 
7. Observe 5S +1, (Sort, Set in order, Shine, Standardize, Sustain, and Safety). 
8. Stewards of environment thru the conduct of research related activities that protects the environment 
9. Involvement in the promotion on Green Technology

RTL COURSE SYLLABUS in MCA300 MASTER’S THESIS 
 
 
 
MSU-IIT 
Vision 
A research university committed to the 
holistic development of the individual 
and society. 
 
Mission 
To provide quality education for the 
sustainable development of the nation 
and the global community. 
 
COLLEGE OF COMPUTER 
STUDIES 
Vision 
A Center of Excellence in Information 
and Communication Technology 
manned by motivated and highly 
competent workforce who adheres to 
Institute policies; equipped with state- 
of-the-art infrastructure; founded on 
relevant instruction, strong culture of 
Research & Extension and enhanced 
resource-generating programs 
producing highly competitive 
graduates imbued with professional 
values. 
 
Mission 
Transform the deserving sector of the 
society i nto highly competitive 
graduates who will respond to the 
needs of the Local and International 
industries for ICT professionals. 
 Course No./Title:  MCA300 MASTER’S THESIS 
Course Credit:  6 units 
Duration: 18 weeks (Semester Year: _______) 
Delivery Mode:  Flexible (Asynchronous/ Synchronous) sessions 
Level: Advanced 
Course Description: This course is an avenue for students to complete their master’s thesis requirements for MSCA program. Students 
must concentrate on finishing their thesis write-up by employing self-discipline and a systematic work attitude. Thesis 
writing is not only an academic endeavor. It is also an intellectual journey. As an academic endeavor one must learn 
the techniques of careful planning, organization, and execution of the research project. As an intellectual journey, one 
should be ready to take risks and to deal with uncertainties and ambiguities in a research undertaking. The thesis is 
a work of original scholarship, designed with guidance from a thesis adviser and thesis committee/panel. 
Learning Culminating 
Outcome: 
  By the end of this course, the students can: defend and submit their master’s thesis.  
1. To demonstrate planning and organization of research work that meets the required timeline of the thesis 
2. To execute the tasks to complete the needed components of the thesis 
3. To communicate the outcome of the research being undertaken through rigorous writing 
4. To present the thesis in the final defense 
Prerequisite: CCC297 Methods of Research 
Co-requisite: None 
Evaluation Criteria: Passing the course requires an overall score of: P 
Course 
Developers/Instructors: 
Prof. Cenie M. Vilela-Malabanan, Ph.D                           
Department of Computer Applications  
cenie.malabanan@g.msuiit.edu.ph/ Consultation hours: 6:00-9:00 PM Weekdays

CCS Commitment 
Integral to the attainment of its 
mission, the College commits itself 
to: 
1. Develop a highly motivated 
versatile ICT workforce. 
2. Offer highly specialized and 
ladderized programs. 
3. Keep abreast with state-of-the-art 
technology. 
4. Develop a strong culture of 
research, extension and production. 
 
CA DEPARTMENT 
 
1.To understand the design & 
development of hardware device and 
software programs through specialized 
skills in Embedded System and Internet 
of Things (IoT). 
 
2.To sharpen the mathematical analysis 
and produce patentable innovations to 
cater the demands of Information and 
Communication Technology (ICT) in 
helping to solve the emerging and 
future global problems. 
 Outcomes for HIGHER 
EDUCATION INSTITUTION:  
Outcomes common to the Master of Science in 
Computer Applications: 
 
Outcome as a State 
University as stipulated in 
CMO 46 s 2012: 
A. To keep abreast of latest 
developments in the specific 
field of practice; 
B. Effectively communicate using 
English and Filipino, orally and 
in writing; 
C. Work effectively and 
independently in multi-
disciplinary and multi-cultural 
teams; 
D. Exemplify professional, social, 
ethical, and environmental 
responsibility; 
E. Preserve and promote “Filipino 
historical and cultural heritage” 
(based on RA 7722); and 
F. Advocate for peace in multi-
cultural settings. 
G. Apply knowledge of mathematics and sciences to 
solve computer electronics problems. 
H. Analyze a problem, formulate and identify solutions 
for computer applications and technology   problems 
using analytical tools appropriate to areas of 
specialization. 
I. Apply design principle using software and firmware for 
broadly defined computer applications. 
J. Implement and evaluate computer application 
systems, components, or processes to meet specific 
needs. 
K. Select and apply appropriate techniques, resources 
and modern computing and ICT tools necessary for 
computer applications practices. 
L. Function effectively as a member or leader of a 
development team recognizing the different roles 
within a team to accomplish a common goal. 
M. Communicate effectively with the computer 
applications community and with society at large 
about complex computer application activities through 
logical writing, presentations, and clear instructions. 
N. Understand and commit to professional ethics and 
responsibilities and norms of computer and cyber 
technology practices. 
O. Recognize the need for and have the ability, to 
engage in independent learning for continual 
development as a technology specialist. 
P. Ability to generate new 
knowledge in the form of 
research or developmental 
projects to support national, 
regional, or local 
development plans

RTL COURSE SYLLABUS in CCC296 ICT FOR PEACE AND DEVELOPMENT 
 
MSU-IIT 
Vision 
A research university committed to the 
holistic development of the individual 
and society. 
 
Mission 
To provide quality education for the 
sustainable development of the nation 
and the global community. 
 
COLLEGE OF COMPUTER 
STUDIES 
Vision 
A Center of Excellence in Information 
and Communication Technology 
manned by motivated and highly 
competent workforce who adheres to 
Institute policies; equipped with state-

producing highly competitive 
graduates imbued with professional 
values. 
 
Mission 
Transform the deserving sector of the 
society into highly competitive 
graduates who will respond to the 
needs of the Local and International 
industries for ICT professionals. 
 Course No./Title:  CCC296 ICT FOR PEACE AND DEVELOPMENT 
Course Credit:  1 unit 
Duration: 18 weeks (Semester Year: _______) 
Delivery Mode:  Blended/Online 
Level: Advanced 
Course Description: The course is designed to examine the latest ICT technologies and its  use and implications to individual, 
organization, and society. It emphasizes on the value of these technologies for the promotion of peace 
and development given the  volatility, uncertainty, complexity, and ambiguity of the world. It puts forward 
the context of Mindanao and how it  influences or influenced by the presence and potentials of these ICT 
technologies. Mainstreaming peace building in the advancement of ICT 
Learning Culminating 
Outcome: 
At the end of the course: 
The students will be able produce a survey of available information and communications technology to be applied a 
given organizational or organization context that assesses the potentials, uses, or implications of those technologies 
to peace and development of a community/organization. 
Prerequisite: BS degree related to ITE program or 1 year experience managing an computer applications, information 
technology and information systems project 
Co-requisite: None 
Evaluation Criteria: Research Paper (Case Study)               – 40% 
Case Studies/Formative Assessment          – 30% 
Readings and Assignment               – 20% 
Participation and related activities               – 10% 
                                                             Total: 100% 
Course 
Developers/Instructors: 
Prof. Rabby Q. Lavilles DIT 
rabby.lavilles@g.msuiit.edu.ph / Consultation hours: 6:00-9:00 PM Weekdays

Classroom Polices: 
1. Observe excellent performance on the following: 
a) Honesty and Integrity; Punctuality/Attendance; Use class time appropriately; Remain in your seat until dismissed by your teacher. 
b) Use technology (i.e., Anycast, Bluetooth, WiFi, etc.) appropriately;  
c) Put cell phones and other noise makers on silent mode or turn them off. If you need to take a call, for some urgent or emergency reason, then 
please let the instructor know before class and then answer the call outside of the classroom. 
d) Follow obediently the computer laboratory policies implemented by the department. 
2. Respect the rights, opinions, ideas, and property of others: 
a) Be courteous.   
b) Raise hand before speaking.  
c) Perform class activities without interrupting/disturbing anyone.   
d) Use laboratory equipment properly to avoid accident, and ensure safety of others. 
3. Take active participation on class discussion, laboratory activities and department/college extracurricular activities 
4. Contribute to discussions by sharing new ideas, innovations and relevant researches 
5. Refrain/avoid inappropriate comments.

C. POLICIES    
1. Your instructor may or may not explicitly check attendance every day. However, if you are caught exceeding your allowable cuts for 
the semester, you may be given a grade of 5.00. 
2. In case you cut, it will be your responsibility to know the material covered for the day. The instructor reserves the right to give 
unannounced quizzes or graded lab exercises at any time. 
3. No makeup tests will be given unless you can present a medical certificate or an immediate member of your family died. Make up 
tests will solely be on the teacher’s discretion. 
4. Playing games is strictly prohibited during class hours. Web browsing and doing email are also prohibited, unless done in connection 
with the current lecture or lab topic and allowed by the teacher. 
5. Use of communication devices is prohibited during class hours. Please turn them off during class. 
6. Class requirements are due during class hours, unless otherwise specified. Late submission will merit deductions as specified by the 
teacher. 
7. Cheating will not be tolerated. Cheating in any requirement will result in a minimum penalty of having a grade of 0 for that 
requirement. Duplicated projects/lab exercises will merit penalties for both the student who copied and the student from whom the 
work was copied. 
8. Additional policies, with due consultation with the students, may be implemented by the teacher to adapt to the class environment. 
Students are advised to be aware of such updates, and to ask their instructor if anything is unclear. 
 
D. Civility in the Classroom 
Students are expected to assist in maintaining a classroom environment that is conducive to learning. To ensure that all students 
have the opportunity to gain from time spent in class, faculty members are encouraged to include a statement in their course syllabi 
relating to behavioral expectations in the classroom.

E. Students with Disabilities 
Any student who, because of a disability, may require special arrangements in order to meet the course requirements should contact 
the instructor as possible to make necessary arrangements. Students must present appropriate verification from Institute Clinic during 
the instructor’s office hours. Please note that instructors are not allowed to provide classroom accommodation to a student until 
appropriate verification from Institute Clinic has been provided.

RTL COURSE SYLLABUS in CCC297 METHODS OF RESEARCH 
MSU-IIT 
Vision 
A research university committed to the 
holistic development of the individual 
and society. 
 
Mission 
To provide quality education for the 
sustainable development of the nation 
and the global community. 
 
COLLEGE OF COMPUTER 
STUDIES 
Vision 
A Center of Excellence in Information 
and Communication Technology 
manned by motivated and highly 
competent workforce who adheres to 
Institute policies; equipped with state- 
of-the-art infrastructure; founded on 
relevant instruction, strong culture of 
Research & Extension and enhanced 
resource-generating programs 
producing highly competitive 
graduates imbued with professional 
values. 
 
Mission 
Transform the deserving sector of the 
society i nto highly competitive 
graduates who will respond to the 
needs of the Local and International 
industries for ICT professionals. 
 Course No./Title:  CCC297 METHODS OF RESEARCH 
Course Credit:  3 units 
Duration: 18 weeks (Semester Year: _______) 
Delivery Mode:  Asynchronous (remotely supervised) with a few synchronous sessions 
Level: Advanced 
Course Description: This course will introduce students to understand and describe the Introduction and Basic Research Concepts, 
Qualitative Research Methods, & Quantitative Research Methods and Statistics, Introduction to Mixed Methods 
Research. Covers Data Mining – Finding the Patterns and Problems in the World of Data. Writing About Quantitative 
Findings, Qualitative or Mixed Methods Findings, And Critically Critiquing Research Reports. 
This course is a prerequisite to Master’s Thesis (MCA300) which discusses the essential requirements to undertake 
a research project. The first four of the five modules are the n ecessary components on understanding the process, 
planning, and designing the research. Overall, students are guided on how to write their proposal which they shall 
present and defend during their proposal hearing. Students have to concentrate on finishing  their thesis proposal by 
employing self-discipline and systematic work attitude. 
Learning Culminating 
Outcome: 
By the end of this course, the student is able:  
1. To understand and describe the Introduction and Basic Research Concepts. 
2. To construct and explain the Qualitative Research Methods, & Quantitative Research Methods and Statistics. 
3. To understand and describe the Introduction to Mixed Methods Research. 
4. To apply the design, analyze and implement Data Mining – Finding the Patterns and Problems in the World 
of Data. Writing About Quantitative Findings, Qualitative or Mixed Methods Findings, And Critically Critiquing 
Research Reports. 
Prerequisite: None 
Co-requisite: None 
Evaluation Criteria: Passing the course requires an overall percent of 60% 
Course 
Developers/Instructors: 
Prof. Joel I. Miano, Department of Computer Applications  
joel.miano@g.msuiit.edu.ph / Consultation hours: 6:00-9:00 PM Weekdays

Grading System 
Rubric 1: For Article Review  
 
  Level  1  Level  2  Level  3  Level  4  
Comprehension and response to 
article (Thinking/ Inquiry)  
10 Marks  
Student lacked clear  
understanding of the article and 
may or may not have expressed a 
personal response.  
Student evidenced some 
understanding of parts of the 
article or did not express a 
personal response.  
Student evidenced considerable 
comprehension  
of the article and articulated a 
thoughtful response.  
Student evidenced clear 
comprehension  
of the article and articulated a 
thoughtful response.  
Summary for Article   
(Knowledge/Understanding)  
 Summarize the main ideas and 
facts in the article.  
  
10 Marks  
No summary is provided OR a 
verbatim of the text is provided. 
Author and source are not named.  
Some details from article are 
missing. Summary  
is not objective OR minimal 
referencing to the article is  
provided. Author OR source are 
not named.  
Most of the main ideas and facts 
from the article are included. 
Summary is presented in 
objective view and referencing to 
the article is provided. Author 
and source are named.  
All main ideas and facts from the 
article are included. Summary is 
presented in objective view and 
referencing to the article is 
provided. Author and source are 
named.  
Presentation of ideas in written 
form (Communication)  
 10 Marks  
Student gave a disorganized 
presentation of ideas in writing with 
main points of article lacking.  
Student vague about main 
points of article.  
Student somewhat engaged the 
reader in highlighted the most of 
the main points of article.  
Student engaged audience in 
organizing his/her ideas and 
highlighted main points of article.

Rubric 3.  For Oral presentation of Cases 
  
Criteria Level 4 Level 3 Level 2 Level 1 
  
Knowledge / Understanding 
 10 Marks 
-knowledge of issue  is 
exceptionally accurate and is 
explained clearly and effectively 
during explanation using details 
and little reliance on notes 
- issue is accurately explained and  uses 
many details and various sources in 
presentation with some reliance on notes 
- issue is explained with some 
accuracy but need more details and 
more variety in sources and less 
reliance on notes 
-issue needs to use more 
accurate information and 
details or examples 
-heavy reliance on notes during 
presentation 
  
Thinking /Inquiry 
  
 10 Marks 
-exceptional critical comments 
and analysis of issue / 
interpretations / impact /  effect 
/ using details, insight, evidence 
from essay and comprehensive 
thought 
-proficient critical comments and analysis 
of issue /interpretations and impact using 
many details and evidence and some 
insight 
-some critical comments given to 
issue and effects 
- more details, insight and critical 
thought needed 
-lack of critical or analytical 
thought in comments and little 
to no insight used 
  
Communication 
 10 Marks 
  
-exceptional delivery and timing 
of information 
-exceptional discussion initiated 
and maintained  to further 
student learning 
  
-proficient delivery and timing of 
information 
-proficient discussion started and 
maintained 
-delivery and timing of information 
needs to be more smooth (too 
much reading) 
-more active interaction and 
discussion 
-poor delivery and timing of 
information 
-discussion needs to be more 
controlled and dynamic 
  
Application 
  
 10 Marks 
- discussion questions are 
exceptionally insightful 
- presenters make critical 
conclusions and connections in 
feedback and answering 
questions 
- powerpoint is exceptionally 
detailed, organized, logical and 
includes images, clear and large 
font 
- discussion questions are insightful 
- presenters make clear conclusions and 
connections in feedback and answering 
questions 
- powerpoint is detailed, organized, 
logical and includes images, clear and 
large font 
- discussion questions are clear but 
need more insightful 
- presenters need to make 
clearer  conclusions and 
connections 
- powerpoint is somewhat 
organized and includes some 
images 
- weak discussion questions 
that that lacked any insight 
- weak conclusions and 
connections 
- powerpoint needs to be more 
organized and logical

Classroom Polices: 
1. Observe excellent performance on the following: 
a) Honesty and Integrity; Punctuality/Attendance; Use class time appropriately; Remain in your seat until dismissed by your teacher. 
b) Use technology (i.e., Anycast, Bluetooth, WiFi, etc.) appropriately;  
c) Put cell phones and other noise makers on silent mode or turn them off. If you need to take a call, for some urgent or emergency reason, then please 
let the instructor know before class and then answer the call outside of the classroom. 
d) Follow obediently the computer laboratory policies implemented by the department. 
2. Respect the rights, opinions, ideas, and property of others: 
a) Be courteous.   
b) Raise hand before speaking.  
c) Perform class activities without interrupting/disturbing anyone.   
d) Use laboratory equipment properly to avoid accident, and ensure safety of others. 
3. Take active participation on class discussion, laboratory activities and department/college extracurricular activities 
4. Contribute to discussions by sharing new ideas, innovations and relevant researches 
5. Refrain/avoid inappropriate comments. 
6. Equality in the use of the laboratory facilities irrespective of gender. 
7. Observe 5S +1, (Sort, Set in order, Shine, Standardize, Sustain, and Safety). 
8. Stewards of environment thru the conduct of research related activities that protects the environment 
9. Involvement in the promotion on Green Technology
